# all analyses were set up in BEAUTI2.4.4 and BEAUTI2.3.2

# The following was first done under StarBeastWithSTACEYops template
# both allele sequences of each individual were assigned to the same taxon
# substitution models were entered, as they resulted from jmodeltest2 (JC=JC69, K80=HKY85, SYM=GTR)
# in case of +G models, 4 gamma categories were added
# in case of +I models, proportion invariant was set to 0.9
# clock model is a strict clock, with a rate of 1 set for the first locus (uce-142), which also happens to be one of the most informative ones. All other clock rates are estimated relatively to this first locus.
# in the priors tab:
# keep Yule model
# birthRate: Log Normal, with M=4.6, S=1.5 (so that 1000 is still in reach - Grahams suggestion)
# clock-rate for all loci should be Log Normal with M=0 and S=1 (only has to be set for one locus, the others can be replaced later in ****xml file****)
# popMean = Log Normal, M=-7, S=2 (you want small values)
# run for 1,000,000,000 generations, logging every 20,000
# all gene trees, log only every 100,000,000 generations (only set it up for one genetree and edit the others in ****xml file****)



# The same with the STACEY template
# copy the block with substitution models from StarBeast file into STACEY file
# for collapseWeight prior, I chose a Gamma distribution with alpha=0.02 and beta=1, preferring small values but which are different form 0

#If BEAST doesn't run because of a likelihood error, add a newick starting tree for all gene trees, which looks like this
 #   <init spec="beast.util.TreeParser" id="NewickTree.t:uce-xxxx_phased" initial="@Tree.t:uce-xxxx_phased" taxa="uce-xxxx_phased" IsLabelledNewick="true" newick="(((((T_pyra1_0,T_pyra1_1),(T_pyra2_0,T_pyra2_1)),((T_pyra3_0,T_pyra3_1),(T_pyra4_0,T_pyra4_1))),(((T_pella5_0,T_pella5_1),(T_pella6_0,T_pella6_1)),((T_pella7_0,T_pella7_1),((T_pella8_0,T_pella8_1),(T_pella9_0,T_pella9_1))))),(Florisuga_0,Florisuga_1))">

#or for species tree:
    <init spec="beast.util.TreeParser" id="NewickTree.t:Species" initial="@Tree.t:Species" taxonset="@taxonsuperset" IsLabelledNewick="true" newick="((((T_pyra1,T_pyra2),(T_pyra3,T_pyra4)),((T_pella5,T_pella6),(T_pella7,(T_pella8,T_pella9)))),Florisuga)">
    </init>



The below actually worked!!
#Below is the complete substitution model code from BEAST2.3.2 (StarBeastWithSTACEYops)
        <distribution id="likelihood" spec="util.CompoundDistribution">
            <distribution id="treeLikelihood.uce-142_phased" spec="TreeLikelihood" data="@uce-142_phased" tree="@Tree.t:uce-142_phased">
                <siteModel id="SiteModel.s:uce-142_phased" spec="SiteModel">
                    <parameter id="mutationRate.s:uce-142_phased" estimate="false" name="mutationRate">1.0</parameter>
                    <parameter id="gammaShape.s:uce-142_phased" estimate="false" name="shape">1.0</parameter>
                    <parameter id="proportionInvariant.s:uce-142_phased" estimate="false" lower="0.0" name="proportionInvariant" upper="1.0">0.0</parameter>
                    <substModel id="hky.s:uce-142_phased" spec="HKY" kappa="@kappa.s:uce-142_phased">
                        <frequencies id="estimatedFreqs.s:uce-142_phased" spec="Frequencies" frequencies="@freqParameter.s:uce-142_phased"/>
                    </substModel>
                </siteModel>
                <branchRateModel id="StrictClock.c:uce-142_phased" spec="beast.evolution.branchratemodel.StrictClockModel">
                    <parameter id="clockRate.c:uce-142_phased" estimate="false" name="clock.rate">1.0</parameter>
                </branchRateModel>
            </distribution>
            <distribution id="treeLikelihood.uce-534_phased" spec="TreeLikelihood" data="@uce-534_phased" tree="@Tree.t:uce-534_phased">
